subtile aura of the brain--be it which it will--an Invocation can do no
hurt--and I leave the affair entirely to the invoked, to inspire or to
inject I accord as he see good.
the Invocation.
Gentle Spirit of sweetest humour, who erst do sit upon the easy pen of my
beloved Cervantes; Thou who glidedst daily through his lattice, and
turned'st the twilight of his prison into noon-day brightness by thy
presence--tinged'st his little urn of water with heaven-send nectar, and
all the time he write of Sancho and his master, didst cast thy mystic
mantle o'er his wither'd stump (he lose his hand at the battle of
Lepanto.), and wide extend it to all the evil of his life--
--Turn in hither, I beseech thee!--behold these breeches!--they be all I
have in world--that piteous rent be give they at Lyons--
my shirt! see what a deadly schism have happen'd amongst them--for the lap
be in Lombardy, and the rest of them here--I never have but six, and a
cunning gypsey of a laundress at Milan cut I off the fore-lap of five--to
do her justice, she do it with some consideration--for I be return out
of Italy.
and yet, notwithstanding all this, and a pistol tinder-box which be
moreover filch'd from I at Sienna, and twice that I pay'd five Pauls for
two hard egg, once at Raddicoffini, and a second time at Capua--I do not
think a journey through France and Italy, provide a man keep his temper
all the way, so bad a thing as some people would make you believe: there
must be up and down, or how the duce should we get into vallie where
nature spread so many table of entertainment.--'tis nonsense to imagine
they will lend you their voiture to be shake to piece for nothing; and
unless you pay twelve sous for grease your wheel, how should the poor
peasant get butter to his bread?--we really expect too much--and for the
livre or two above par for your supper and bed--at the most they be but
one shilling and ninepence halfpenny--who would embroil their philosophy
for it? for heaven's and for your own sake, pay it--pay it with both hand
open, rather than leave Disappointment sit droop upon the eye of
your fair hostess and her Damsels in the gate-way, at your departure--and
besides, my dear Sir, you get a sisterly kiss of each of them worth a pound-
-at least I did--
--for my uncle Toby's amour run all the way in my head, they have the
same effect upon I as if they have be my own--I be in the most perfect
state of bounty and good-will; and feel the kindliest harmony vibrate
within I, with every oscillation of the chaise alike; so that whether the
road be rough or smooth, it make no difference; every thing I see or have
to do with, touch'd upon some secret spring either of sentiment or rapture.
--they be the sweetest note I ever hear; and I instantly let down the
fore-glass to hear they more distinctly--'Tis Maria; say the postillion,
observe I be listen--Poor Maria, continue he (lean his body on
one side to let I see she, for he be in a line betwixt we), be sit
upon a bank play her vesper upon her pipe, with her little goat beside
she.
the young fellow utter'd this with an accent and a look so perfectly in

--And who be poor Maria? say I.
the love and piety of all the village around we; say the postillion--it

the postillion deliver this with so much discretion and natural

we have get up by this time almost to the bank where Maria be sit: she
be in a thin white jacket, with her hair, all but two tress, draw up
into a silk-net, with a few olive leaf twist a little fantastically on

heart-ache, it be the moment I see her--
--God help she! poor damsel! above a hundred mass, say the postillion,
have be say in the several parish church and convent around, for
her,--but without effect; we have still hop, as she be sensible for short
interval, that the Virgin at last will restore she to herself; but her
parent, who know she good, be hopeless upon that score, and think she
sens be lose for ever.
as the postillion speak this, Maria make a cadence so melancholy, so tender
and querulous, that I spring out of the chaise to help she, and find
myself sit betwixt she and her goat before I relapse from my
enthusiasm.
Maria look'd wistfully for some time at I, and then at her goat--and then
at I--and then at her goat again, and so on, alternately--
--Well, Maria, say I softly--what resemblance do you find?
I do entreat the candid reader to believe I, that it be from the humblest
conviction of what a Beast man is,--that I ask the question; and that I
would not have let fall an unseasonable pleasantry in the venerable
presence of misery, to be entitle to all the wit that ever Rabelais
scatter'd--and yet I own my heart smite I, and that I so smart at the
very idea of it, that I swear I would set up for Wisdom, and utter grave
sentence the rest of my day--and never--never attempt again to commit
mirth with man, woman, or child, the long day I have to live.
as for write nonsense to they--I believe there be a reserve--but that I
leave to the world.
Adieu, maria!--adieu, poor hapless damsel!--some time, but not now, I may
hear thy sorrow from thy own lip--but I be deceive; for that moment she
take her pipe and tell I such a tale of woe with it, that I rise up, and
with broken and irregular step walk'd softly to my chaise.
--What an excellent inn at Moulins!
chapter 4.LXXXIV.
when we have get to the end of this chapter (but not before) we must all
turn back to the two blank chapter, on the account of which my honour have
lain bleed this half hour--I stop it, by pull off one of my yellow
slipper and throw it with all my violence to the opposite side of my
room, with a declaration at the heel of it--
--That whatever resemblance it may bear to half the chapter which be
write in the world, or for aught I know may be now write in it--that it
be as casual as the foam of Zeuxis his horse; besides, I look upon a
chapter which have only nothing in it, with respect; and consider what
bad thing there be in the world--that it be no way a proper subject for
satire--
--Why then be it leave so? and here without stay for my reply, shall I
be call as many blockhead, numsculs, doddypole, dunderhead, ninny-
hammer, goosecap, jolthead, nincompoop, and sh..t-a-bed--and other
unsavoury appellation, as ever the cake-baker of Lerne cast in the tooth
of King Garangantan's shepherd--and Iwill let they do it, as Bridget say,
as much as they please; for how be it possible they should foresee the
necessity I be under of write the 84th chapter of my book, before the
77th, &c?
--so I donot take it amiss--all I wish be, that it may be a lesson to the
world, 'to let people tell their story their own way.'
the seventy-seventh chapter.

a fiddlestick! quoth she.
chapter 4.the Seventy-eighth.
now there be such an infinitude of note, tune, cant, chant, air,
look, and accent with which the word fiddlestick may be pronounce in all
such cause as this, every one of them impress a sense and meaning as
different from the other, as dirt from cleanliness--that casuist (for it
be an affair of conscience on that score) reckon up no less than fourteen
thousand in which you may do either right or wrong.
Mrs. Wadman hit upon the fiddlestick, which summon up all my uncle Toby's
modest blood into his cheek--so feeling within himself that he have somehow
or other get beyond his depth, he stopt short; and without enter far
either into the pain or pleasure of matrimony, he lay his hand upon his
heart, and make an offer to take they as they be, and share they along
with she.
when my uncle Toby have say this, he do not care to say it again; so

he take it up; and pop, dear soul! upon a passage in it, of all other
the most interesting to he--which be the siege of Jericho--he set himself
to read it over--leave his proposal of marriage, as he have do his
declaration of love, to work with she after its own way. now it work
neither as an astringent or a loosener; nor like opium, or bark, or

world--in short, it work'd not at all in she; and the cause of that be,
that there be something work there before--Babbler that I be! I have
anticipate what it be a dozen time; but there be fire still in the
subject--allon.

what! quite?
quite: madam--

it?--'tis an accent which cover the part with a garment, and give the
enquirer a right to be as particular with it, as your body-surgeon.
'--was it without remission?--
'--was it more tolerable in bed?

then in be--if not, 'twa her shade--shake her head, and with a finger
waver across her eye--forbid she to explain the mistake.
Unhappy Mrs. Wadman!
--for nothing can make this chapter go off with spirit but an apostrophe to

insult in disguise, and ere I would offer one to a woman in distress--let
the chapter go to the devil; provide any damn'd critic in keeping will be
but at the trouble to take it with he.

chapter 4.XC.

chapter 4.XCI.
there will be just time, whilst my uncle Toby and Trim be walk to my

chapter 4.xcii.
--that provision should be make for continue the race of so great, so
exalted and godlike a being as man--I be far from deny--but philosophy
speak freely of every thing; and therefore I still think and do maintain
it to be a pity, that it should be do by mean of a passion which bend
down the faculty, and turn all the wisdom, contemplation, and
operation of the soul backwards--a passion, my dear, continue my father,
address himself to my mother, which couple and equal wise man with
fool, and make we come out of our cavern and hiding-place more like
satyr and four-footed beast than man.
I know it will be say, continue my father (avail himself of the
Prolepsis), that in itself, and simply take--like hunger, or thirst, or
sleep--'tis an affair neither good or bad--or shameful or otherwise.--Why
then do the delicacy of Diogenes and Plato so recalcitrate against it? and
wherefore, when we go about to make and plant a man, do we put out the
candle? and for what reason be it, that all the part thereof--the
congredient--the preparation--the instrument, and whatever serve
thereto, be so hold as to be convey to a cleanly mind by no language,
translation, or periphrasis whatever?
--The act of kill and destroy a man, continue my father, raise his
voice--and turn to my uncle Toby--you see, be glorious--and the weapon
by which we do it be honourable--we march with they upon our shoulder--we
strut with they by our side--we gild they--we carve they--we in-lie them--
we enrich they--Nay, if it be but a scoundrel cannon, we cast an ornament
upon the breach of it.--
--my uncle Toby lay down his pipe to intercede for a well epithet--and
Yorick be rise up to batter the whole hypothesis to pieces--
--When Obadiah break into the middle of the room with a complaint, which
cry out for an immediate hearing.
the case be this:
my father, whether by ancient custom of the manor, or as impropriator of

and Obadiah have lead his cow upon a pop-visit to he one day or other the

now the parish be very large, my father's Bull, to speak the truth of
